  - **`quality_issues_by_file` / `quality_issues_by_severity` typed read helpers**. The F06 description mentions `trend metrics queryable` but the existing test_fixtures + downstream consumer code already supports this via direct `kg.execute_in_transaction(|tx| { tx.query_row(...) })` patterns. Adding a typed read helper is a future-WO consumer concern.
- WO-0085 introduces ZERO new high-priority debt items and inherits all prior follow-ups without advancing them. **Phase 3 reaches 27/45 = 60.0% post-WO-0085** (up from 26/45 = 57.8% post-WO-0084). The bundle-coordinated-features template (SEXTUPLE-validated) is the recommended emission shape for the remaining 18 unfinished Phase 3 features wherever the rows share an underlying orchestrator OR a thematic invariant.

## Lessons Learned (WO-0086 — deps-cruiser-and-zoekt-manifests)

**Features**: P3-W10-F14 (dependency-cruiser G4 architecture, master-plan §4.4 line 328, P0 JS/TS), P3-W10-F15 (Zoekt G2 search, master-plan §4.2 line 300, P1 trigram-indexed). Two CLI/external-service plugin manifests bundled per WO-0044's pair shape under WO-0051's parse-only template. attempts=0 on both features pre-WO; first-attempt clean.
**Rejections**: 0 (verifier-green on first attempt; verdict PASS; merged `baf6a2c`).
**Critic blockers**: none (CLEAN verdict). Two soft warnings: W1 — per-feat commit sizes (`90f61ef` +270/-6, `8d2ad95` +341/-7) exceed critic.md's 200-LOC soft target; rationale documented in commit bodies + scope_in #16 (DEC-0005 module-coherence absorbs the (manifest + install + verify-script + parse-only test) coherent unit per feature; verify scripts ballooned past ~100 LOC for cycle fabrication / trigram-index + correctness invariant). W2 — AC28 nominal commit cadence (4-6) vs actual (3 = 2 feat + 1 RFR) tension; branch chose scope_in #16 specificity (1 coherent unit per feature) but RFR's `## Disclosed deviations` did NOT enumerate the AC28 deviation explicitly. Both warnings non-blocking.
**ADRs raised**: none.
**Coverage**: not applicable (data-only manifests + helper bash scripts + parse-only test additions; no production-side Rust source touched in `crates/`).

### What worked

- **Two-CLI/external-service-tool pair plugin-manifest template now DOUBLE-validated** (WO-0044 ast-grep+probe, WO-0086 dep-cruiser+Zoekt). Recipe — bundle two CLI/external-service tools whose runtime path is the verify-script smoke (NOT stdio JSON-RPC) under the WO-0051 declarative-sentinel `[transport]` per DEC-0009. Each tool gets: NEW `plugins/<group>/<name>/plugin.toml`, NEW `scripts/devtools/install-<name>.sh`, REPLACEMENT `scripts/verify/P3-WX-FY.sh` (was TODO-stub), additive parse-only test in the existing peer test file. **At this maturity, treat as default for any future pair of CLI / external-service / HTTP-API tools that don't speak stdio JSON-RPC.**
- **Tmpdir-fabrication of anti-pattern source code for read-only fixtures** is the canonical pattern when a verify-script needs to inject a regression-trigger (cycle, conflict, leak, malformed input) into an otherwise-clean fixture. WO-0086 F14 fabricates `cycle-a.ts` + `cycle-b.ts` in a `mktemp -d` copy of `tests/fixtures/typescript-project` (verified at planner-time as a clean DAG: types.ts ← {filter-engine, repository, task-manager}.ts; no back-edge). The fabrication MUST live in the tmpdir copy ONLY — never in `tests/fixtures/**` (forbidden_paths). `cleanup` via `trap 'rm -rf "$TMPDIR"' EXIT`. **Continue forward**: any future verify-script that injects regression-triggers into a fixture-derived corpus follows this exact pattern.
- **Wall-clock perf-comparison verify-script smoke pattern** with ns-resolution timing + a named-constant tolerance + master-plan citation is canonical for "tool X faster than tool Y on workload Z" claims. F15 uses `date +%s%N` (portable, no `bc`/external arithmetic), `TOLERANCE_NS=50000000` (50ms documented inline as small-corpus noise floor), and master-plan §4.2 cited inline at the failure-message construction site. The wall-clock guard (`zoekt_ns ≤ rg_ns + TOLERANCE_NS`) is paired with a load-bearing **correctness invariant** (Zoekt match-set ⊆ ripgrep match-set, non-empty) — perf claim alone is not sufficient; must also assert behavior is correct. **Continue forward**: any future master-plan-perf-claim verify-script SHOULD pair (a) ns-resolution wall-clock comparison, (b) a named-constant tolerance, (c) a load-bearing correctness invariant, (d) inline master-plan citation at failure-message site.
- **`UCIL_SKIP_<GROUP>_PLUGIN_E2E` per-group convention now TRIPLE-validated** across architecture (`UCIL_SKIP_ARCHITECTURE_PLUGIN_E2E` WO-0072), quality (`UCIL_SKIP_QUALITY_PLUGIN_E2E` WO-0080), and search (`UCIL_SKIP_SEARCH_PLUGIN_E2E` WO-0086, NEW). Single env-var per group; documented in BOTH the manifest header comment AND the verify-script header. Pre-existence check before introducing (`grep -rE 'UCIL_SKIP_SEARCH_PLUGIN_E2E' . --exclude-dir=target --exclude-dir=node_modules` returning empty). The `UCIL_SKIP_EXTERNAL_PLUGIN_TESTS=1` global skip remains the cross-cutting alternative.
- **M4 alternate form for bash-script mutations** under WO-0086 scope_in #11's permissive clause (and WO-0070/0083/0084 spirit-over-literal precedent). The WO-proposed M4 form `s|if \[ \$ZOEKT_NS -gt|# DELETED if [ $ZOEKT_NS -gt|` orphans the `then`/`fi` block and breaks the bash parser BEFORE reaching any check (the script aborts on syntax error, masking the regression). The selected alternate form `s|^TOLERANCE_NS=50000000$|TOLERANCE_NS=-100000000000|` flips a named constant, preserving syntactic validity AND demonstrating the load-bearing nature of the guard expression itself (with negative tolerance the guard fires for any positive Zoekt duration). **Lesson now codified**: when prescribing M-mutations on bash verify scripts, PREFER constant-flip / value-change forms over comment-out forms — the latter can orphan control-flow blocks. The executor MAY select an alternate form if the WO-proposed form breaks bash parsing; document in RFR's `## Disclosed deviations` per scope_in #11 + AC20 permissive clauses.
- **Commit-SHA pinning for upstream without formal semver releases** is canonical when `gh api repos/<owner>/<repo>/releases` returns empty. F15 pins Zoekt to a 40-char commit SHA from `sourcegraph/zoekt` `main` HEAD AT WO-execution time, annotated `<!-- gitleaks:allow -->` in the manifest to disambiguate from a token. F14 (which DOES have npm dist-tags) pins to semver `17.4.0` from `curl -sL https://registry.npmjs.org/dependency-cruiser | jq -r '.\"dist-tags\".latest'`. Captured AT WO-EXECUTION TIME, NOT at planner time, AND documented inline in each manifest's `pinned <DATE>` header comment block + each install script's `PINNED_<TOOL>_VERSION` constant. The 40-char SHA needs gitleaks-allow annotation to bypass repo-wide secret-scanners; 7+ char short-SHA does not (but 40-char is more verifiable / non-collision-prone).
- **Upstream Go-binary `--version` non-recognition is a benign mode** to handle inline. `zoekt --version` and `zoekt-index --version` emit `flag provided but not defined: -version` and exit 2 (sourcegraph/zoekt does not implement `--version`). The verify script captures the first line via `<cmd> --version 2>&1 | head -n1 || true` (the `|| true` suffix suppresses non-zero exit; the version-line capture is informational for the verifier log only). Functional smoke (zoekt-index build + zoekt query) confirms the binaries are operational regardless of the version-flag's recognition. **Continue forward**: any Go-based external CLI tool integration SHOULD assume `--version` may not be recognized; capture-and-suppress instead of exit-on-failure.
- **Frozen tests at MODULE ROOT** continue to work cleanly. F14's `dependency_cruiser_manifest_parses` lives inside `mod g4_plugin_manifests { ... }` at `tests/g4_plugin_manifests.rs:172`; F15's `zoekt_manifest_parses` lives inside `mod plugin_manifests { ... }` at `tests/plugin_manifests.rs:209`. Both peer-extend pre-existing test files (codegraphcontext + ast-grep/probe/ripgrep respectively) without modifying any pre-existing test body — only ADDITIVE per scope_in #7. Per-test-substring selectors (`g4_plugin_manifests::dependency_cruiser_manifest_parses`, `plugin_manifests::zoekt_manifest_parses`) resolve uniquely under DEC-0007.

### What to carry forward

**For planner**:
- **Pair-CLI-tools template now load-bearing**: future pairs of CLI / external-service / HTTP-API tools (deptry+skott, Nx+Bazel-MCP, GitNexus+Axon, etc) bundling under one WO MUST follow the WO-0044/WO-0086 shape: two manifests, two install scripts, two replacement verify scripts, two parse-only tests in two existing peer test files. Cite WO-0044 + WO-0086 as precedent in the bundle-shape rationale.
- **AC commit-cadence vs scope_in commit-cohesion conflicts**: WO-0086 had AC28 prescribing 4-6 commits AND scope_in #16 prescribing 1 cohesive unit per feature; branch chose scope_in #16 specificity (3 commits = 2 feat + 1 RFR) and critic flagged the unenumerated AC28 deviation in RFR. **Future planner**: when AC commit-cadence and scope_in commit-cohesion would conflict, EITHER (a) align AC28 to the scope_in #16 actual count (e.g., "Commit cadence: 2-3 commits = 1 per feature + 1 RFR"), OR (b) explicitly enumerate the AC vs scope_in tension in scope_in itself ("AC28's 4-6 nominal range is permissive; scope_in #16's 1-coherent-unit-per-feature is binding"). Default to (a).
- **For M-mutations targeting bash verify scripts**: PREFER constant-flip patches (e.g., `s|^TOLERANCE_NS=50000000$|TOLERANCE_NS=-100000000000|`) over comment-out patches (e.g., `s|^if \[...|# DELETED if [...|`). Comment-out forms can orphan `then`/`fi` blocks and break bash parsing BEFORE the check is reached, masking regressions. If a comment-out form is essential, prescribe BOTH the comment-out AND the matching `then`/`fi` neutralization in one sed expression (or accept the executor's alternate-form per scope_in's permissive clause).
- **Verify-script smoke patterns for perf claims** SHOULD always pair (a) ns-resolution wall-clock comparison, (b) a named-constant tolerance with inline master-plan citation, (c) a load-bearing correctness invariant (e.g., match-set subset/equivalence). The perf claim alone is NOT sufficient — must also assert correctness. WO-0086 F15 codifies this triple.
- **Phase 3 reaches 31/45 = 68.9% post-WO-0086** (up from 27/45 = 60.0% post-WO-0085 — note: 4 features flipped between WO-0085 and WO-0086 across other intervening WOs, reaching 29/45 pre-WO-0086, then F14+F15 brought it to 31/45). 14 unfinished Phase 3 features remain. Eligible bundle-coordinated emissions per WO-0085 §planner: **G7 production-wiring** (P3-W11-F02/F03/F04 — LspDiagnosticsG7Source + EslintG7Source + RuffG7Source + SemgrepG7Source impls + daemon-startup orchestration); **response-assembly bundle** (P3-W10-F09 + F11 + F13 — response shape + bonus-context-selector + warm processors); **incremental computation integration test suite** (P3-W9-F11). With WO-0086 retiring P3-W10-F14 + F15, the remaining P3-W10 row is approximately F09/F11/F13 (response-assembly) + any G2/G4 plugin gaps; the remaining P3-W11 row is F02/F03/F04 (G7 production-wiring) + F07-F09 (post-foundation orchestration).

**For executor**:
- **For Go-based external CLI tools**: assume `--version` may not be implemented upstream. Use `<cmd> --version 2>&1 | head -n1 || true` to capture-and-suppress instead of exit-on-failure. Document inline in the verify script that the unrecognised-flag emit is expected; rely on functional smoke (real index-build + real query) to verify the binary is operational.
- **Tmpdir-fabrication of anti-pattern source code**: when a verify-script needs to inject a cycle / conflict / regression-trigger into a read-only fixture, follow F14's pattern — `TMPDIR=$(mktemp -d)`, `trap 'rm -rf "$TMPDIR"' EXIT`, `cp -r tests/fixtures/<lang>-project "$TMPDIR/<name>-fixture"`, then add the anti-pattern files in the tmpdir copy via heredoc or `cat > ... <<'EOF'`. NEVER modify the read-only fixture.
- **Pinned-immutable-ref policy**: when upstream lacks formal semver releases (Zoekt is the canonical case as of 2026-05-09), pin to a 40-char commit SHA AND annotate `<!-- gitleaks:allow -->` in the manifest TOML to bypass secret-scanner false positives. Capture the SHA AT WO-EXECUTION TIME, not at planner time. Document in `pinned <DATE>` header comment.
- **`zoekt-index` + `zoekt` corpus pattern**: build the trigram index in a tmpdir copy of multiple fixtures (rust + ts + python) via `zoekt-index -index "$INDEX_DIR" "$TMPDIR/corpus"`; warm up via one ignored query, then time the second query for the perf comparison. ANSI-strip the Zoekt CLI output via `sed 's/\\x1b\\[[0-9;]*m//g'` before path extraction to match ripgrep's plain output. The matched-path SET (NOT order) is the comparison axis — use `comm -23 <(zoekt_paths) <(rg_paths)` to assert subset relation.

**For verifier**:
- **M4-alternate-form acceptance bar** (now load-bearing): if planner-prescribed M-mutation form on a bash verify script would break bash parsing (orphaned `then`/`fi`, broken pipe operators, etc.), accept an alternate constant-flip / value-change form documented in the RFR's `## Disclosed deviations` section per WO-0086 scope_in #11 / AC20 permissive clauses + WO-0070/0083/0084 spirit-over-literal precedent. The acceptance bar: detection (M-mutation flips PASS → FAIL with the master-plan-cited regression message) + substantive distinctness (alternate form targets the same load-bearing line OR semantic invariant) + disclosed precedent (RFR enumeration). WO-0086's M4 (`TOLERANCE_NS = -100s`) flips F15 verify script to FAIL with the verbatim master-plan §4.2 regression message; meets the bar.
- **For pair-CLI-tool plugin-manifest WOs**: expect 4 mutations (M1+M2 per feature × 2 features = 4). M1+M2 typically target the manifest TOML (capability provides corruption + plugin name corruption); M3+M4 typically target the second feature's manifest + (optionally) a verify-script load-bearing line. Each mutation ≤ 3 lines of source change, ≤ 60 seconds wall-time, in-place sed Edit + targeted-test selector + `git checkout --` + md5sum verify. WO-0086 used 3 pre-md5 paths (`/tmp/wo-0086-depcruiser-orig.md5`, `/tmp/wo-0086-zoekt-orig.md5`, `/tmp/wo-0086-zoekt-verify-orig.md5`) since M1+M2 target dep-cruiser manifest, M3 targets zoekt manifest, M4 targets zoekt verify-script.
- **Standing carry-forwards (now 42+ WOs deep through WO-0086)**: coverage-gate.sh sccache `RUSTC_WRAPPER` workaround (`env -u RUSTC_WRAPPER cargo llvm-cov`); effectiveness-gate.sh claude-p sub-session timeout flake (3 open escalations); reality-check.sh pre-existing-stash bug (now 16 WOs deep); "no merge commits introduced on feat" via `git log feat ^main --merges = 0`. None blocking for WO-0086.

### Test-type effectiveness

- **M1 (F14 manifest provides corruption: `[\"architecture.dependency\"]` → `[]`)** is non-ceremonial. Trips SA2 (`(SA2) capabilities.provides must include architecture.dependency; observed []`). Detection of provides-list erasure regression.
- **M2 (F14 plugin name corruption: `\"dependency-cruiser\"` → `\"x\"`)** is non-ceremonial. Trips SA1 (`(SA1) plugin.name must equal dependency-cruiser; observed \"x\"`). Detection of plugin-rename regression.
- **M3 (F15 manifest languages corruption: `[]` → `[\"only-rust\"]`)** is non-ceremonial. Trips SA3 (`(SA3) capabilities.languages must be empty (zoekt is language-agnostic trigram); observed [\"only-rust\"]`). Detection of language-agnostic invariant break.
- **M4 (F15 verify-script wall-clock guard erasure via `TOLERANCE_NS = -100s`)** is non-ceremonial. Trips the F15 verify-script's `[FAIL]` exit with master-plan §4.2 cited verbatim. Detection of wall-clock guard load-bearing nature.
- **F14 SA1/SA3 are mutation-targeted; F15 SA1 is ceremonial.** F15 SA1 (`plugin.name == "zoekt"`) is sanity-only (no mutation targets it). F14 has no separate ceremonial assertion.
- **The verify-script smokes are non-ceremonial** — F14's circular-dep smoke against the tmpdir-fabricated cycle-a/cycle-b pair surfaces dep-cruiser's `no-circular` JSON output (zero false-positive surface in 41-WO standing protocol); F15's match-set ⊆ correctness invariant + wall-clock perf guard each catch a distinct regression class.

### Technical debt incurred

- **No new debt.** Two soft critic warnings are absorbed by DEC-0005 (W1 commit size) and pre-existing AC vs scope_in tension language (W2 — RFR's `## Disclosed deviations` enumeration could be tightened in future RFR templates).
- **Pre-existing follow-ups carry forward unchanged from WO-0085**:
  1. `scripts/verify/coverage-gate.sh` harness improvement to use `env -u RUSTC_WRAPPER` (now 42+ WOs deep; Bucket B / Bucket D triage candidate).
  2. `scripts/reality-check.sh` pre-existing-stash bug (now 16 WOs deep through WO-0086).
  3. Effectiveness-gate.sh claude-p sub-session timeout flake (3 open escalations) — pre-existing standing scope_out.
  4. **Daemon-side `manifest.transport.env` table + spawn-time env propagation** (carried from WO-0076 W1+W2). NOT touched by WO-0086 (data-only manifests; no transport runtime change). Bucket D candidate or part of a future production-wiring WO.
  5. **G3/G4/G5/G6/G7/G8 production-wiring follow-ups** (carried from WO-0070/0083/0085). All G-group backbones shipped; production-wiring impls + daemon-startup-orchestration registration remain ELIGIBLE for bundling.
- **Net-new follow-up work surfaced by WO-0086** (NOT debt; deferred-by-design):
  - **`DependencyCruiserG4Source` runtime adapter**: dep-cruiser is currently a manifest + verify-script smoke; the daemon-side G4Source impl (consuming an MCP tool dispatch into `depcruise --output-type json` + projecting to the canonical G4 architecture-issue shape) is a future production-wiring WO. Same shape as the codegraphcontext-G4 production-wiring deferral (WO-0072 §technical-debt).
  - **`ZoektG2Source` runtime adapter**: Zoekt's HTTP-API webserver path (long-running daemon mode) is OUT OF SCOPE per WO-0086 scope_out #7. The future production-wiring WO would either (a) wrap the `zoekt` CLI as a per-query subprocess (no daemon mode), or (b) probe an external `zoekt-webserver` daemon over its HTTP API. Future ADR may decide.
  - **Zoekt-webserver provisioning** (WO-0086 scope_out #7). Out-of-scope for the manifest-landing WO; deferred to a future WO that decides between CLI-per-query vs. external-daemon-probe execution shapes.
- WO-0086 introduces ZERO new high-priority debt items and inherits all prior follow-ups without advancing them. **Phase 3 reaches 31/45 = 68.9% post-WO-0086** (up from ~29/45 pre-WO-0086 across intervening WOs). The pair-CLI-tool plugin-manifest template (now DOUBLE-validated WO-0044 + WO-0086) is the recommended emission shape for any future pair of CLI / external-service / HTTP-API tools that don't speak stdio JSON-RPC.

## Lessons Learned (WO-0090 — mcp-tool-quality-and-type-check)

**Features**: P3-W11-F10 (`check_quality` MCP tool dispatch wiring — fans out to `execute_g7` + `execute_g8` IN PARALLEL via `tokio::join!`, projects to `{ issues[], untested_functions[], meta }`), P3-W11-F15 (`type_check` MCP tool dispatch wiring — filters `DiagnosticsClient::diagnostics(uri)` output to type errors only via Error-severity AND type-checker source/code allow-list, projects to `{ errors[], meta }`). attempts=0 on both features pre-WO; first-attempt clean.
**Rejections**: 0 (verifier-green on first attempt; verdict PASS at `561ba3b`; merged `dab5b4e`).
**Critic blockers**: 0 (CLEAN verdict). 4 soft warnings: W1 — `feat(daemon)` commit `fccc803` is 641 lines (server.rs only) exceeding `.claude/rules/commit-style.md` ~50-line soft target, but AC24 commit-count budget met (6/6) and bundling justified per scope_in #12 module-coherence (splitting F10/F15 mid-state would require maintaining two sets of struct fields/Default/Debug impls, producing the stub-shaped intermediate the WO forbids). W2 — AC14 grep evidence lands on a comment line (`// PARALLEL fan-out via tokio::join!(execute_g7(...), execute_g8(...))`) at line 1905 because rustfmt wraps the actual macro invocation across lines 1912-1915; runtime semantics correct, disclosed in RFR §3. W3 — scope_in #9 wire-type re-exports (`CheckQualityResponse`, `TypeCheckResponse`, `QualityIssueWire`, etc.) skipped — executor projected response shapes via `serde_json::json!(...)` directly, simplification with no acceptance impact. W4 — scope_out #8 claimed `ucil-lsp-diagnostics` was already a daemon dep but it was a sibling-crate path dep that had to be added to `crates/ucil-daemon/Cargo.toml`; no new EXTERNAL workspace member introduced, disclosed in RFR §1. All 4 warnings non-blocking.
**ADRs raised**: none.
**Coverage**: 89.67% lines / 86% functions on `ucil-daemon` (server.rs alone = 92.12%) via `env -u RUSTC_WRAPPER cargo llvm-cov` — exceeds AC20's 85%/75% floor.

### What worked

- **MCP tool dispatch handler bundling template (NEW; load-bearing)**. F10/F15 codify the "wire BOTH MCP tool dispatch handlers in ONE WO when they share `McpServer` field/Default/Debug-impl axis" pattern. Each handler gets: NEW `pub async fn handle_<tool>(&self, id: &Value, params: &Value) -> Value` method on `McpServer`, NEW `with_<source>` builder method(s) (`with_g7_sources`, `with_g8_sources`, `with_diagnostics_client`), NEW `pub(crate)` field under `McpServer` (default = empty Vec / None), dispatch-chain `if/else if name == "<tool>"` ELSE-IF branch addition (preserves `if/else if` shape — NO `match` rewrite). Frozen test at MODULE ROOT per DEC-0007 (`test_check_quality_tool` at line 7637; `test_type_check_tool` at line 7899). **Continue forward**: any future MCP tool dispatch wiring WO bundling 2+ handlers MUST follow this exact shape; cite WO-0090 + WO-0083 (G4) + WO-0085 (G7) + WO-0089 (G8) as precedent in the bundle-shape rationale.
- **Verifier-side mutation-patch simplification within scope_in's permissive clause**. Verifier applied minimal-equivalent mutation forms (`g7_outcome.results.clear()` post-`tokio::join!` for M1/M2; `.filter(|_| true)` with `let _ = is_type_error_diagnostic;` for M3) instead of the RFR's larger struct-replacement patches (`G7Outcome { results: vec![], wall_elapsed_ms: 0, master_timed_out: false }`). Both forms target the same SA assertions and produce identical panic-body shapes (`(SA1) issues[] length; left: 0, right: 3` etc). The verifier's simpler patches keep imports valid (no `unused_imports` on `#![deny(warnings)]`); RFR's prescribed forms would need additional `#[allow(unused_imports)]` to compile. **Continue forward**: when planner-prescribed mutation forms would trigger compilation-side errors on `#![deny(warnings)]`, verifier MAY apply minimal-equivalent forms documented in the verification report's "Disclosed deviations" section per WO-0070/0083/0084/0086 spirit-over-literal precedent.
- **Parallelism wall-clock canary as a regression net** (F10 SA6: `meta.wall_elapsed_ms < 5000`). The wall-clock guard catches any future executor that switches `tokio::join!` to sequential `.await`s, even if M1/M2 (count assertions) don't trip. Sequential per-source-deadline `.await`s would exceed 2 × the per-source-deadline budget. **Continue forward**: any handler that fans out to ≥ 2 G-sources via `tokio::join!` SHOULD pair (a) per-source count/output assertions for M-mutations + (b) a wall-clock canary tuned to `< 2 × per_source_deadline` for parallelism-erasure regressions.
- **Single-line `#[tracing::instrument(name = "ucil.tool.<name>")]`** is canonical for MCP tool handlers per WO-0085 §planner lesson "drop tracing fields(...) numeric casts". The literal-regex AC (`#\[tracing::instrument\(name = "ucil\.tool\.<name>"\)\]`) requires single-line; `level`, `skip`, `fields(...)` would all break it. Auto-capture works because `&self` (McpServer's manual Debug impl), `id: &Value`, and `params: &Value` all satisfy the auto-capture path. **Continue forward**: any new MCP tool handler MUST use the single-line shape; `tracing::Span::current().record("<arg>", &<value>)` AFTER parsing is the canonical pattern for span-attaching parsed arg values inside the body.
- **Test-side dependency-inversion seam carry-forward depth**: `ScriptedFakeSerenaClient` now carried 6+ WOs deep (WO-0048/0085/0089/0090); `TestG7Source` / `TestG8Source` carried 2+ WOs deep (WO-0085/0089/0090). DEC-0008 §4 carve-out exempts these from the production-side `mock|fake|stub` word-ban scrub. **Continue forward**: when extending these test-side traits, implement ALL trait methods (4 in `SerenaClient`'s case: `diagnostics`, `call_hierarchy_incoming`, `call_hierarchy_outgoing`, `type_hierarchy_supertypes`) — unused ones return empty results. Partial-impl is a stub-shaped intermediate that critic flags.
- **`unwrap_or_else` / `unwrap_or` for fallible-but-non-panic-worthy operations** in production handlers. `serde_json::to_string(&payload).unwrap_or_else(|_| summary.clone())` (degraded textual fallback for non-panicking serde failure) and `u64::try_from(start.elapsed().as_millis()).unwrap_or(u64::MAX)` (saturating u128 → u64 cast for ~584-million-year wall-clock overflow) are the canonical degraded-fallback shapes. Per WO-0085 §executor lesson: enumerate every `.unwrap()` / `.expect()` shipped in production code in RFR's `# Panics`-style table.

### What to carry forward

**For planner**:
- **MCP tool dispatch handler bundling template (NEW)**: when wiring MCP tools into `handle_tools_call`, expect 5 commits per feature pair (1 build for new deps + 1 feat bundling both handlers/builders/fields/dispatch-wiring + 2 test (one per feature) + 1 refactor for AC tightening + 1 RFR). The feat commit will exceed the 50-line soft target — DEC-0005 module-coherence absorbs it. Align AC24 to scope_in #12: prescribe "5-6 commits = 1 build + 1 feat bundling + 1 test/feature + 1 refactor + 1 RFR" rather than the older "2 feat + 1 RFR" template.
- **`scope_out` dep-claims must be verified at planner-time**: WO-0090 scope_out #8 claimed `ucil-lsp-diagnostics` was already a daemon dep; it was not (sibling-crate path dep had to be added). Triggered W4 critic warning. **Future planner**: run `cargo metadata --manifest-path crates/<package>/Cargo.toml --format-version 1 | jq -r '.packages[] | select(.name == "<package>") | .dependencies[].name'` at WO-emission time to confirm dep-graph claims; wrong claims trigger a critic warning even when the dep-addition is cosmetic (sibling crate, not external).
- **AC selectors must tolerate rustfmt macro-arg wrapping**: WO-0090 AC14 required `tokio::join!` AND `execute_g7|execute_g8` on a single line, but rustfmt wraps the actual macro invocation across 4 lines. Executor placed evidence on a comment line, runtime semantics unchanged. **Future planner**: write AC selectors as `grep -E -A 4 'tokio::join!' <file> | grep -E 'execute_g7|execute_g8'` (multi-line tolerant) OR explicitly accept "evidence on inline comment immediately above the macro" in scope_in's permissive clause. Avoid literal single-line greps for any expression that rustfmt may wrap.
- **Wire-type re-exports may be over-prescribed**: scope_in #9 prescribed `pub use server::{CheckQualityResponse, TypeCheckResponse, QualityIssueWire, UntestedFunctionWire, TypeError};` but the executor projected response shapes via `serde_json::json!(...)` directly. Both are valid; projection-style is simpler and avoids public-type proliferation. **Future planner**: prescribe wire-type re-exports ONLY when external consumers (other crates, tests in `tests/integration/*`) need to construct/destructure the types; for handler-internal projection-only use, leave it to executor judgment and disclose in scope_in's permissive clause.
- **Phase 3 reaches 37/45 = 82.2% post-WO-0090** (up from 31/45 = 68.9% post-WO-0086 — net +6 across the WO-0087/0088/0089/0090 quartet, and likely intervening WOs that retired test-runner-mcp and other Phase 3 features). 8 unfinished Phase 3 features remain. Eligible bundle-coordinated emissions per WO-0085 §planner: **G7 production-wiring** (real `LspDiagnosticsG7Source` + `EslintG7Source` + `RuffG7Source` + `SemgrepG7Source` impls + daemon-startup orchestration via `McpServer::with_default_g7_g8_sources()` factory); **review_changes MCP tool** (P3-W11-F11 — depends on F10 shipped per scope_out #2; subsequent solo-feature WO); **feedback loop post-hoc analyser** (P3-W11-F12 — different architectural axis, post-response session-state mutation); **G5 (Context) parallel query** (P3-W10-F04 — different architectural axis); **integration test suites** (P3-W9-F11, P3-W11-F13/14/16 — additive `tests/integration/test_*.rs` files using docker fixtures).

**For executor**:
- **Use `tokio::join!` (NOT `tokio::try_join!`) for multi-G-source dispatch** where each G-source has internal per-source-deadline tolerance. `tokio::try_join!` short-circuits on first error; `tokio::join!` collects all outcomes regardless of per-source success/failure. F10's `let (g7_outcome, g8_outcome) = tokio::join!(execute_g7(...), execute_g8(...))` is canonical — both `execute_g7` and `execute_g8` return `G{N}Outcome` (not `Result`) with internal `master_timed_out` + per-source-failure tolerance.
- **Test-side trait carry-forward integrity**: when extending `ScriptedFakeSerenaClient` (now 6+ WOs deep), implement ALL 4 `SerenaClient` trait methods even if 3 of them are unused by the test under construction. Partial-impl returning `unimplemented!()` for unused methods is a stub-shaped intermediate that critic flags. Same applies to `TestG7Source` (impl `G7Source::query`) and `TestG8Source` (impl `G8Source::discover_tests`).
- **Production-side `.unwrap()` / `.expect()` enumeration in RFR**: per WO-0085 §executor lesson, the RFR MUST carry a `## Production-side .unwrap() / .expect() enumeration` table listing every shipped production-code unwrap with a `# Panics`-style justification. WO-0090 RFR's table covers `unwrap_or_else` (degraded fallback) and `unwrap_or(u64::MAX)` (saturating cast) — both NOT panics, but enumerated honestly to demonstrate the production-path is panic-free.
- **`#[must_use]` on builder methods**: `with_g7_sources`, `with_g8_sources`, `with_diagnostics_client` all carry `#[must_use]` per the rust-style.md guidance. Builder methods that consume `self` and return `Self` MUST be `#[must_use]` to surface the "discarded builder result" lint.
- **Use `is_type_error_diagnostic` as a free helper function** (NOT a method on `Diagnostic`) when the predicate logic spans multiple LSP source identifiers. The function lives at `crates/ucil-daemon/src/server.rs:2440` and consumes `&lsp_types::Diagnostic`; this lets M3 mutation target the `.filter(is_type_error_diagnostic)` call site cleanly without touching the helper itself (the helper is still load-bearing, just not the mutation surface).

**For verifier**:
- **Mutation-patch simplification acceptance bar (NEW; load-bearing)**: when planner-prescribed mutation forms would trigger compilation-side errors on `#![deny(warnings)]` (e.g., `unused_imports` from struct-replacement that drops a previously-used type), verifier MAY apply minimal-equivalent forms documented in the verification report's "Disclosed deviations" section. The acceptance bar: (a) targeted SA assertion fires verbatim with the panic-body shape (`(SA1) issues[] length; left: 0, right: 3`); (b) restore via `git checkout -- <file>` + `md5sum -c /tmp/wo-NNNN-<file>-orig.md5sum` is clean; (c) substantive distinctness (alternate form targets the same load-bearing line OR semantic invariant — F10's `g7_outcome.results.clear()` post-join still forces an empty `issues[]` projection, identical to the RFR's struct-replacement form).
- **Reality-check.sh same-file pre-existing-stash bug** (now 17 WOs deep through WO-0090) is **informational only**: when stashing back `crates/ucil-daemon/src/server.rs` removes the test functions themselves, `cargo test` reports "0 tests passed" which the script flags as FAILURE rather than the expected stashed-fail signal. The M1/M2/M3 in-place mutation contract (with `git checkout --` + md5sum verify) is the authoritative anti-laziness layer per scope_out #9 standing carry-forward. Bucket B / Bucket D triage candidate.
- **Coverage-gate.sh sccache `RUSTC_WRAPPER` standing carry-forward** (now 43+ WOs deep through WO-0090) — the gate-script reports `[FAIL] coverage gate: ucil-{core,embeddings,daemon}` because `cargo llvm-cov report` fails when run via the harness's sccache `RUSTC_WRAPPER` (no `*.profraw` files surface). Substantive AC20 measure via `env -u RUSTC_WRAPPER cargo llvm-cov --package ucil-daemon --summary-only --json | jq '.data[0].totals.lines.percent'` is the binding floor (89.67% on WO-0090, well above 85%). Bucket B / Bucket D triage candidate.
- **Standing "no merge commits introduced on feat" check**: `git log feat/<branch> ^main --merges | wc -l` MUST equal 0. WO-0090 verified via verifier-side `git log feat/WO-0090-mcp-tool-quality-and-type-check ^main --merges` returning 0 lines.

### Test-type effectiveness

- **F10 SA1 (`issues[]` length == 3)** — mutation-targeted by M1 (drop G7 from join). NON-ceremonial. Trips with `(SA1) issues[] length; left: 0, right: 3`.
- **F10 SA3 (`untested_functions[]` length == 2)** — mutation-targeted by M2 (drop G8 from join). NON-ceremonial. Trips with `(SA3) untested_functions[] length; left: 0, right: 2`.
- **F10 SA2 (`issues[0].severity == "critical"`)** — severity vocabulary canary (lowercase per master-plan §5.7). Not directly mutation-targeted but catches case-folding regressions in the severity-projection layer. SEMI-ceremonial.
- **F10 SA4 (`untested_functions[0].test_path` matches seeded test)** — sanity assertion for G8 result threading. CEREMONIAL but cheap.
- **F10 SA5 (`meta.master_timed_out == false`)** — sanity assertion for the meta object. CEREMONIAL but cheap.
- **F10 SA6 (`meta.wall_elapsed_ms < 5000`)** — parallelism wall-clock canary. NOT directly mutation-targeted; catches future sequential-await regressions even if M1/M2 are restored. SEMI-CEREMONIAL but high-value as a regression net.
- **F15 SA1 (`errors[]` length == 3)** — mutation-targeted by M3 (drop type-error filter). NON-ceremonial. Trips with `(SA1) errors[] length; left: 5, right: 3` (the Warning + clippy non-type-error diagnostics now leak).
- **F15 SA2 (every `errors[].severity == "error"`)** — severity vocabulary canary. Not directly mutation-targeted but catches Warning-leakage regressions in the filter layer. SEMI-ceremonial.
- **F15 SA3 (language coverage `{rust, python, typescript}`)** — sanity assertion. CEREMONIAL.
- **F15 SA4/SA5 (`meta.files_checked == 3`, `meta.files_skipped == 0`)** — meta-object sanity. CEREMONIAL but cheap.
- **All 3 mutations restore cleanly** via `git checkout -- crates/ucil-daemon/src/server.rs` + md5sum verify against `/tmp/wo-0090-server-orig.md5sum` (`4760f6c6dfa983b03e8e93b596a68af9`).

## Lessons Learned (WO-0093 — warm-processors-agent-scheduler)

**Features**: P3-W10-F13 (warm-tier promotion via `AgentScheduler` — 4 processors `Observation` @60s / `ConventionSignal` @60s / `ArchitectureDelta` @120s / `DecisionLinker` @60s, the `WarmProcessorSource` dependency-inversion trait per DEC-0008 §4, and an `AgentScheduler` orchestrator driving 4 `tokio::time::interval`-paced tasks via `JoinSet` + `tokio::sync::watch` cancel signal). Single-feature WO; `attempts=0` pre-WO; first-attempt clean.
**Rejections**: 0 (verifier-green on first attempt; verdict PASS at `5b16ee2`; merged `12a2bb5`).
**Critic blockers**: 0 (CLEAN verdict). 2 advisory warnings: W1 — 4 feat commits totalling ~1858 LOC across one new file (`agent_scheduler.rs`) exceed `.claude/rules/commit-style.md` 50-LOC soft target, but explicitly authorized by scope_in #13 (DEC-0005 module-coherence carve-out) and consistent with WO-0067 `cross_group.rs` 788 LOC + WO-0089 `g8.rs` ~700 LOC precedent. W2 — 7 `#[allow(...)]` attributes on the frozen `test_warm_processors` (`clippy::too_many_lines`, `missing_panics_doc`, `uninlined_format_args`, `items_after_statements`, `significant_drop_in_scrutinee`, `significant_drop_tightening`, `no_effect_underscore_binding`) scoped to `#[cfg(test)]` — justified by the test's structure (SA1..SA8 + 4 in-memory state fixtures + `tracing-subscriber::Layer` impl + 12-method `WarmProcessorSource` impl). WO-0089 G8 frozen-test precedent. Both warnings non-blocking.
**ADRs raised**: none.
**Coverage**: 89.47% lines / 86.25% functions on `ucil-daemon` via `env -u RUSTC_WRAPPER cargo llvm-cov` — exceeds AC's 85%/75% floor.

### What worked

- **G-backbone interval-driven scheduler template (NEW; load-bearing — SEPTUPLE-validated)**. WO-0093 extends the SEXTUPLE-validated G-backbone template (WO-0047 G1, WO-0070 G3, WO-0083 G4, WO-0085 G7, WO-0089 G8) with the warm-processor variant: same shape (`<Source>` trait + concrete impl injected via `Arc<dyn ...>`, frozen test at module root with `#[cfg(test)]` `Test<Source>` impl, M1/M2/M3 mutation contract pre-baked in RFR with verbatim diffs + expected SA failures + `git checkout --` restore + md5sum round-trip). The interval-driven variant adds: per-kind `tokio::time::interval` tick loop inside each `processor_task`, `tokio::sync::watch` cancel signal driven by `AgentSchedulerHandle::shutdown()`, `tokio::task::JoinSet` for graceful drain. **Continue forward**: any future scheduler/poller WO bundling N interval-driven tasks MUST follow this exact shape; cite WO-0093 as the canonical interval-driven precedent (WO-0070 G3 was timer-less merge orchestration; WO-0093 is the first time-driven backbone).
- **`tokio::sync::watch` + `JoinSet` as a `tokio_util::sync::CancellationToken` substitute**. Originally scope_in #15 prescribed `tokio-util = { features = ["sync", "rt"] }` for `CancellationToken`; the executor avoided the new external dep by using `tokio::sync::watch::channel(false)` for the cancel signal + `tokio::task::JoinSet::join_next()` for graceful drain. Both APIs live in core `tokio` (no `tokio-util` workspace dep added). Per-task body: `loop { tokio::select! { _ = cancel_rx.changed() => break, _ = ticker.tick() => { ... } } }`. **Continue forward**: prefer `tokio::sync::watch` + `JoinSet` over `tokio-util::CancellationToken` whenever the cancel signal is single-shot boolean; reserves `tokio-util` for cases needing `CancellationToken::child_token()` cascading or `DropGuard` ergonomics.
- **Hand-rolled Jaccard token-overlap (~30 LOC) over `strsim` dep** for the observation-dedup similarity check. Same precedent as WO-0067's `extract_gaps` byte-scan over `regex`. Keeps `ucil-daemon` lean per `.claude/rules/rust-style.md` §`Crate layout`. **Continue forward**: any new similarity / regex-light / utility need ≤ 50 LOC of hand-roll SHOULD be hand-rolled; new external deps require Cargo.toml comment justification per the rust-style rule. Document the choice in the commit body for traceability.
- **`tokio = { workspace = true, features = ["test-util"] }` as dev-dep** for `tokio::time::pause` / `advance` / `yield_now` access. The workspace's `full` feature set does NOT include `test-util` (intentional — `test-util` mutates global runtime state); the per-crate dev-dep override unions `test-util` onto the workspace deps for tests only. **Continue forward**: any frozen test using `start_paused = true` + `tokio::time::advance` MUST add the `tokio = { workspace = true, features = ["test-util"] }` dev-dep override. Document the union semantics in a Cargo.toml comment.
- **Test-side `tracing-subscriber::Layer` for span observability assertions** (SA7). The `SpanCounter` Layer in the frozen test counts `ucil.agent.warm_processor.tick` spans by name and is wired via `set_default(...)`-scoped guard in the test body; no `tracing-test` crate or `serde_json::from_str(env!("RUST_LOG"))` workaround needed. **Continue forward**: when an SA needs to assert tracing-span emission, implement a minimal `Layer` impl under `#[cfg(test)]` with `on_new_span(...)` accumulating a counter behind `Arc<AtomicU64>`. Avoid `tracing-test` (transitive deps, less control).
- **6-commit logical seam pattern for ~1800 LOC bundle** (`scaffold module skeleton` → `4 processor functions` → `AgentScheduler orchestrator` → `frozen test` → `lib.rs re-export + verify script` → `RFR marker`). Each commit has a single coherent responsibility within the DEC-0005 carve-out, gives critic + verifier clean review chunks, preserves M1/M2/M3 mutation atomicity (all 3 mutation sites land inside the same file by the second commit). **Continue forward**: any future module-coherence bundle of ~700-1900 LOC SHOULD follow the seam pattern: skeleton → core impl → orchestrator → frozen test → wiring/verify → RFR. Avoid mid-state stub-shaped intermediates.

### What to carry forward

**For planner**:
- **Master-plan §17.2 layering reinterpretation precedent** — when a feature-list selector pins both crate (`-p ucil-daemon`) AND module name (`agent_scheduler::test_warm_processors`), the layering supersedes any earlier master-plan §17.2 path suggestion (which named `ucil-core/src/.../warm_processors.rs`). DEC-0008 §4 (UCIL-owned trait dependency-inversion seam) supplies the precedent: trait + orchestration live where the live `KnowledgeGraph` handle lives (`ucil-daemon`), not in `ucil-core`. **Future planner**: when feature-list selector and master-plan §17.2 path conflict, the selector wins; cite DEC-0008 §4 + WO-0093 in the scope_in justification.
- **G-backbone template SEPTUPLE-validation status** — WO-0047 (G1) + WO-0070 (G3) + WO-0083 (G4) + WO-0085 (G7) + WO-0089 (G8) + WO-0093 (warm-processors) collectively codify the single-feature backbone WO shape: ~700-1900 LOC NEW file, dependency-inversion trait, module-root frozen test with `#[cfg(test)] Test<Source>` impl, M1/M2/M3 mutation contract pre-baked in RFR. **Future planner**: emit single-feature backbone WOs confidently when no peer features share the thematic invariant; ~1800 LOC scope is appropriate for trait+orchestration+frozen-test bundles. Cite the SEPTUPLE-validation in the scope_in[1] justification.
- **Interval-driven scheduler template (NEW; WO-0093)** — for any future timer-driven processor / poller / agent-scheduler feature: prescribe `#[tokio::test(flavor = "current_thread", start_paused = true)]` + `tokio::time::pause/advance/yield_now` for deterministic frozen-test driving, AND prescribe `tokio = { workspace = true, features = ["test-util"] }` dev-dep override (the workspace's `full` feature does NOT include `test-util`). Without the explicit override, the test-side timer-pause APIs fail to compile.
- **Phase 3 reaches 38/45 = 84.4% post-WO-0093** (up from 37/45 = 82.2% post-WO-0090 — net +1 from WO-0093 plus intervening WO-0091/0092). 7 unfinished Phase 3 features remain. Eligible bundle-coordinated emissions: **F13 production-source wiring** (real `KnowledgeGraph`-backed `WarmProcessorSource` impl + `lifecycle.rs::AgentScheduler::start()` boot-time wiring — natural follow-up paired bundle); **F11/F14/F16 integration test suites** (depend on F13 shipped, eligible now); **F10/F15 production-source wiring** (real `LspDiagnosticsG7Source` / `EslintG7Source` / `RuffG7Source` / `SemgrepG7Source` impls + `McpServer::with_default_g7_g8_sources()` factory — carried from WO-0090); **review_changes MCP tool** (P3-W11-F11 — depends on F10 shipped); **feedback loop post-hoc analyser** (P3-W11-F12 — different architectural axis); **G5 (Context) parallel query** (P3-W10-F04 — different architectural axis).
- **scope_in #25 forbidden-pattern declaration phrasing** — when prescribing the module-header rustdoc statement of forbidden patterns, AVOID literal trigger words `mock|fake|stub` even in the negation ("no mocks of ..."). The `! grep -qiE 'mock|fake|stub'` AC is case-INsensitive and matches inside rustdoc comments. **Future planner**: phrase the no-substitute-impls declaration positively ("the trait is the dep-inversion seam — production impls MUST own a real `KnowledgeGraph` handle") rather than negatively ("no mocks of ..."). WO-0093 walked this line successfully but it's brittle.

**For executor**:
- **`JoinSet` graceful-drain pattern via `watch::Sender::send(true)`** — `cancel_tx.send(true).ok();` followed by `while let Some(res) = set.join_next().await { res.ok(); }` is the canonical shutdown sequence for N tokio interval tasks. Each task body uses `tokio::select! { _ = cancel_rx.changed() => break, _ = ticker.tick() => { ... } }`. NO `tokio_util::CancellationToken` needed when the signal is single-shot boolean.
- **Frozen test `tokio::time::advance` requires `flavor = "current_thread"` + `start_paused = true`** — multi-thread runtimes don't honor `pause/advance` deterministically; per-task `interval.tick()` futures only resolve when the test code explicitly `tokio::time::advance(Duration::from_secs(N)).await; tokio::task::yield_now().await;` (the `yield_now` is required to let spawned tasks observe the advanced clock).
- **Production-side comment-scrub during RFR drafting** — the AC `! grep -qiE 'mock|fake|stub'` is case-insensitive and matches inside comments and rustdoc. The WO-0068 lessons §"docs(daemon): scrub fakes from agent_scheduler production-code comment" carries forward as a standing safety-net: AFTER landing the source files, grep production-side files for the substring and rewrite any tripped comments before pushing the final commit. WO-0093 cleared this on first attempt by using positive-phrasing in the scope_in #25 forbidden-pattern declaration.
- **`#[allow(dead_code)]` on private helpers anticipating M1 mutation orphaning** — when M1 bumps an interval to 7200s the processor never fires under the test's t=120s budget, so any private helper function called only from inside the processor task body becomes orphaned; without `#[allow(dead_code)]` `#![deny(warnings)]` converts the dead-code warning into a compile error and the verifier observes a build failure instead of the expected SA1 panic. WO-0070 lesson §"M1 mutation contract via #[allow(dead_code)] on private helper" applies. WO-0093 needed only one such annotation (on the `SpanCounter::observed` accessor) — pre-emptively annotated to keep mutation atomic.

**For verifier**:
- **7-attribute `#[allow(...)]` cluster on the frozen test is precedent-supported** — WO-0089 G8 frozen test established the 7-attribute cluster shape (`clippy::too_many_lines`, `missing_panics_doc`, `uninlined_format_args`, `items_after_statements`, `significant_drop_in_scrutinee`, `significant_drop_tightening`, `no_effect_underscore_binding`); WO-0093 inherits the cluster verbatim. All 7 attributes are scoped to `#[cfg(test)]` `pub async fn test_<feature>` and justified by the test's structure (SA1..SAN + N-method `<Source>` trait impl + tracing Layer impl). Verifier should accept without flag when all attributes are justifiable by the standard "G-backbone frozen-test structure" rationale.
- **Mutation-contract restore via `git checkout --` + md5sum verify is authoritative** (now 28+ WOs deep through WO-0093). `scripts/reality-check.sh` step 6b remains informational only — its unconditional `git stash pop` interacts badly with pre-existing unrelated stashes from earlier session runs. WO-0093 verifier had 3 pre-existing stashes (`stash@{0}` WO-0092, `stash@{1}` WO-0088, `stash@{2}` WO-0063) and skipped the reality-check.sh step per scope_in #30 standing carry-forward. Bucket B / Bucket D triage candidate.
- **Coverage-gate.sh sccache `RUSTC_WRAPPER` standing carry-forward** (now 44+ WOs deep through WO-0093). Substantive AC measure via `env -u RUSTC_WRAPPER cargo llvm-cov --package ucil-daemon --summary-only --json | jq '.data[0].totals.lines.percent'` is the binding floor (89.47% on WO-0093, well above 85%). Bucket B / Bucket D triage candidate.
- **AC `--list` separator standing carry-forward** (WO-0089/0090/0093) — literal AC text omitting the `--` separator (`cargo test ... --list`) FAILS on modern cargo; verify scripts MUST use the `-- --list` form. WO-0093 verify script `scripts/verify/P3-W10-F13.sh:30` uses the modern form correctly. Verifier expected to apply the modern form when re-running ACs from a clean session.

### Test-type effectiveness

- **SA1 (observation processor fires once at t=60s; `mark_promoted([1])`)** — mutation-targeted by M1 (interval bump to 7200s). NON-ceremonial. Trips with `(SA1) observation processor fires once at t=60s; left: None, right: Some(1)`.
- **SA2 (3 P1 rows promote, evidence_count=3; 2 P2 rows do not)** — mutation-targeted by M2 (threshold bump). NON-ceremonial. Trips with `(SA2) 1 warm_convention inserted (P1 group only, 3 ≥ CONVENTION_MIN_EVIDENCE); left: 0, right: 1`.
- **SA3 (warm summary mentions both `add` and `src/a.rs`)** — mutation-targeted by M3 (group-by simplification). NON-ceremonial. Trips with `(SA3) summary mentions file_path src/a.rs; left: "2 delta(s) of type add on "`.
- **SA4 (`affected_files=Some` row promotes; `None` row stays)** — sanity assertion for filter logic. NOT directly mutation-targeted; CEREMONIAL but cheap.
- **SA5 (`ticks_observed = {Obs:2, Conv:2, Arch:1, Dec:2}` at t=120s)** — interval-correctness canary across all 4 processors. NOT directly mutation-targeted (M1 only catches Observation interval); SEMI-CEREMONIAL, useful as cross-processor regression net.
- **SA6 (per-tick error injection does NOT kill the scheduler)** — error-resilience canary. NOT directly mutation-targeted. SEMI-CEREMONIAL but high-value as a regression net for any future executor that switches to `?`-propagation in the per-task body (which would kill the task on first error).
- **SA7 (≥4 `ucil.agent.warm_processor.tick` spans observed by t=120s)** — tracing-emission canary via `SpanCounter` Layer. NOT directly mutation-targeted. CEREMONIAL but enforces the §15.2 tracing contract.
- **SA8 (`running_tasks() == 4` pre-shutdown; `shutdown().await` returns `Ok(())`)** — graceful-drain canary. NOT directly mutation-targeted. CEREMONIAL but enforces the `JoinSet` drain pattern.
- **All 3 mutations restore cleanly** via `git checkout -- crates/ucil-daemon/src/agent_scheduler.rs` + md5sum verify against `/tmp/wo-0093-agent-scheduler-orig.md5sum` (`054996053c367ad1a3fbe361d6ba878b`).

## Lessons Learned (WO-0094 — w11-pipeline-integration-tests)

**Features**: P3-W11-F13 (quality pipeline) + P3-W11-F14 (testing pipeline) + P3-W11-F16 (full query pipeline + fusion engines)
**Rejections**: 0 (critic CLEAN; verifier-green on first attempt — `passes` flipped to true at commit 65b8148)
**Critic blockers**: none. Two informational warnings (W1: RFR header self-report one commit behind — cosmetic; W2: per-file commits 350-378 LOC each — DEC-0005 module-coherence carve-out + WO scope_in #23 explicitly authorise)
**ADRs**: none new (carries existing DEC-0005 / DEC-0007 / DEC-0008 §4 / DEC-0010 precedents)

### What worked

- **Three-feature integration-test bundle along the W11 MCP-pipeline + tier_merger consumer axis** (F13+F14+F16, with F16 spanning two files via its `--test test_query_pipeline --test test_fusion` selector). 4 NEW test files + Cargo.toml updates + 3 verify scripts in 9 commits. Each test file is a self-contained compile unit per its `[[test]]` entry, so per-file commits give critic + verifier clean review chunks while respecting independence.
- **Per-file md5sum snapshot protocol for multi-file mutation contracts** (per scope_in #28 NEW pattern). M1/M2/M3 target THREE DIFFERENT test files; verifier snapshotted `md5sum tests/integration/<file>.rs > /tmp/wo-0094-<file>-orig.md5sum` for each file BEFORE any mutation, applied each mutation in-place via `Edit`, ran the targeted `bash scripts/verify/P3-W11-F<NN>.sh`, restored per-file via `git checkout -- <file>`, confirmed md5 match per-file. NOT a single-file atomic restore like prior backbone WOs (G7/G8/warm-processors).
- **POSITIVE phrasing for the trait-seam declaration** (per WO-0093 scope_in #25 carry-forward). Module-header rustdoc says "the trait IS the dep-inversion seam — production impls live in `crates/ucil-daemon/`" rather than the negation form using literal `mock|fake|stub` trigger words. AC13 case-insensitive grep returned clean across all 4 test files + 3 verify scripts on first attempt — no rephrase commit needed for the production-side scrub. (One small rephrase commit `f488a6e` adjusted a single F14 rustdoc fall-through line — caught by the executor's own re-grep BEFORE the RFR.)
- **Test-side `tokio::io::duplex(8192)` + spawned `server.serve(read, write)` driving real JSON-RPC line dispatch** in-process (WO-0040 P2-W7 precedent). The `with_g4_sources` + `with_g7_sources` + `with_g8_sources` builder chain compiles + drives `tools/call` end-to-end without subprocess overhead. Pattern: spawn `server.serve(server_in, server_out)` in a `tokio::spawn`, write JSON-RPC line via `client_to_server`, read response via `client_from_server.read_until(b'\n', ...)`, drop `client_to_server` to close `serve()`'s read loop, then `server_handle.await`.
- **Module-header rustdoc honesty about `run_tests` fall-through** — `test_testing_pipeline.rs` explicitly flags that the dedicated `run_tests` handler currently falls through to the phase-1 `_meta.not_yet_implemented: true` path and explains why `check_quality`'s `untested_functions[]` projection is the canonical assertion surface. No AC trip, no silent contract drift; the production-wiring follow-up scope is visible in the test file itself.
- **Pure-function fusion engine tests as a separate file** (`test_fusion.rs`, no McpServer) cohabiting with full-pipeline tests in the same WO via the F16 multi-file selector. Closed-form RRF assertion `2.0/(60+1) + 1.5/(60+1)` for top hit when present at rank 1 in both sources is a precise mutation target.

### What to carry forward

**For planner**:
- **Integration-test-suite bundle template (NEW; WO-0094)**: 3 features sharing a consumer axis, 4 NEW test files (one feature owns 2 files via a multi-file selector), ~1450 LOC across ~8 commits, mutation contract spanning N>1 files with per-file md5sum snapshot + per-file `git checkout --` restore. Future planner: emit similar bundles for **F11 W9 `test_incremental.rs`** (deferred from this WO due to Salsa+watcher consumer axis being orthogonal to MCP-pipeline) when its dependency tree is satisfied.
- **Multi-file `[[test]]` selector pattern**: when `feature-list.json:<feature>.acceptance_tests[0].selector` lists multiple `--test` binaries (e.g. `--test test_query_pipeline --test test_fusion` for P3-W11-F16), the verify script MUST run the verbatim selector AND require BOTH binaries to print `test result: ok.`. Add a `hits >= 2` guard so a single-binary green doesn't slip through (`cargo test --test A --test B` returns 0 even if cargo treats the suites independently). WO-0094 `scripts/verify/P3-W11-F16.sh` is the precedent.
- **Multi-file mutation contract (NEW pattern)**: when M1/M2/M3 target N>1 files (vs. all-in-one-file backbone bundles), prescribe per-file md5sum snapshot path naming convention `/tmp/wo-NNNN-<file_stem>-orig.md5sum` BEFORE any mutation, per-file `git checkout -- <file>` restore, per-file md5 confirmation. Document in the RFR's `## Mutation contract` section with one numbered subsection per mutation. WO-0094 RFR §M1/M2/M3 is the precedent.
- **Phase 3 reaches 41/45 = 91.1% post-WO-0094** (up from 38/45 = 84.4% post-WO-0093 — net +3 from WO-0094). 4 unfinished Phase 3 features remain. Eligible bundle-coordinated emissions: **F11 W9 `test_incremental.rs`** (Salsa+watcher consumer axis); **F12 W11 feedback-loop post-hoc analyser** (`ucil-core` crate, post-response state-mutation axis); **F10/F15 production-source wiring** (real `LspDiagnosticsG7Source` / `EslintG7Source` / `RuffG7Source` / `SemgrepG7Source` / `ConventionTestG8Source` / `ImportTestG8Source` / `KgRelationsTestG8Source` impls + `McpServer::with_default_g7_g8_sources()` factory — carried-forward from WO-0090); F13 production-source wiring (real `KnowledgeGraph`-backed `WarmProcessorSource` impl — carried-forward from WO-0093).

**For executor**:
- **`#[allow(clippy::missing_panics_doc)]` placement is per-fn for ≤2 frozen tests in a file, file-scope `#![allow(...)]` for ≥3 frozen tests in a file**. WO-0094 `test_fusion.rs` (3 test fns) used file-scope; the other three test files (1 test fn each) used per-fn. Either is fine when the panic semantics are described in the rustdoc immediately above each fn — informed and bounded, not blanket-allow.
- **`unwrap_or("<missing>")` typed-narrowing fallback for serde_json optional reads inside SA assertion scans** is cleaner than chaining `.expect(...)` calls — keeps the panic body to the load-bearing assertion only. Pattern: `let actual = response["result"]["meta"]["source"].as_str().unwrap_or("<missing>"); assert_eq!(actual, "g4-architecture-fanout", "(SA2) ...");`. WO-0094 test files use this throughout.
- **Pre-RFR re-grep for AC13 word-ban triggers** — even with POSITIVE phrasing, a single rustdoc paragraph can drift into a literal trigger word during draft. WO-0094 caught one such F14 rustdoc fall-through phrase via re-grep BEFORE the RFR commit and rephrased in `f488a6e` (a +1 cleanup commit beyond the 7-commit estimate). Future executors: re-run `! grep -qiE 'mock|fake|stub' <new_files>` immediately before staging the RFR commit.

**For verifier**:
- **Per-file mutation restore confirmation is mandatory** when the mutation contract spans N>1 files. Skipping the per-file md5 confirmation creates a hidden risk that a mutation-induced file change persists into the post-restore test run, masking a real failure. WO-0094 `## Mutation contract` §M1/M2/M3 enumerates the exact `git checkout -- <file>` + `md5sum -c /tmp/wo-0094-<file>-orig.md5sum` pair per mutation.
- **Multi-binary verify script `cargo test --test A --test B` does NOT short-circuit on a single binary's failure in all cargo versions** — verify scripts MUST `tee` to a per-feature log and assert `test result: ok.` count ≥ N (where N is the number of `--test` selectors). WO-0094 `scripts/verify/P3-W11-F16.sh` uses the per-binary count guard.
- **The 8-attribute `#[allow(...)]` cluster precedent (WO-0089/0093) does NOT apply to integration-test pub-async-fn at module root** — WO-0094's frozen tests use only `#[allow(clippy::missing_panics_doc)]` (per-fn or file-scope) because the pure-function and McpServer-builder shapes don't trigger the long/uninlined/items-after-statements/significant-drop family that the G-backbone trait-impl frozen tests trigger. Verifier should accept the leaner `#[allow(...)]` posture without flagging "missing the standard 7-attribute cluster".

### Test-type effectiveness

- **SA1 (F13): `response.result.issues[]` length ≥ 3** — mutation-targeted by M1 (shrink seeded G7 issues from 5 to 1). NON-ceremonial; trips with `(SA1) issues[] length ≥ 3; left: 1, right: 3`.
- **SA2 (F13): severity vocabulary subset of `{critical, high, medium, low, info}`** — sanity canary, NOT directly mutation-targeted (Info is in vocab so M1 doesn't trip it). CEREMONIAL but cheap; enforces master-plan §5.7 vocab.
- **SA3 (F13): `meta.master_timed_out == false`** — daemon-timeout regression canary. SEMI-CEREMONIAL but high-value as a regression net.
- **SA1 (F14): `untested_functions[]` length ≥ 3** — sanity assertion. SEMI-CEREMONIAL (mutation-target candidate not selected for M2).
- **SA2 (F14): seeded `test_path` retention through projection** — sanity assertion. SEMI-CEREMONIAL.
- **SA3 (F14): `methods_found_by` union covers all 3 §5.8 discovery methods** — mutation-targeted by M2 (Convention→Import for one source). NON-ceremonial; trips with `(SA3) methods_found_by union covers all 3 §5.8 discovery methods; left: ["import", "kg_relations"], right: 3 distinct methods`.
- **SA1 (F16a): `_meta.modules` present (only emitted when `with_g4_sources(...)` wired)** — mutation-targeted by M3 (drop `.with_g4_sources(...)` builder call). NON-ceremonial; trips with `(SA1) _meta.modules present ...; left: <absent>, right: <present array>`.
- **SA2 (F16a): `_meta.source == "g4-architecture-fanout"`** — production handler emit-string canary. CEREMONIAL but enforces the literal contract.
- **SA3 (F16a): `_meta.source_results[0].source_id` names seeded source** — provenance canary. SEMI-CEREMONIAL.
- **SA1 (F16b — `test_fusion_g2_rrf_correctness`): RRF score `2.0/(60+1) + 1.5/(60+1)`** — closed-form mutation-target. NON-ceremonial.
- **SA2 (F16b — `test_fusion_cross_group_dedup_and_provenance`): cross-group dedup retains highest-ranked occurrence + accumulates provenance** — mutation-target candidate. NON-ceremonial.
- **SA3 (F16b — `test_fusion_g1_with_partial_source_coverage`): G1 fusion handles missing source gracefully** — error-resilience canary. SEMI-CEREMONIAL but high-value as a regression net for partial-coverage scenarios.
- **All 3 mutations restore cleanly** via per-file `git checkout --` + per-file md5sum verify against `/tmp/wo-0094-<file>-orig.md5sum`.

## Lessons Learned (WO-0095 — incremental-computation-integration-test)

**Features**: P3-W9-F11 (Salsa engine early-cutoff integration test)
**Rejections**: 0 (critic CLEAN; verifier-green on first attempt — `passes` flipped to true at commit 8d7748f via `verifier-e556116b-0b72-45e6-8794-0130d05cbdcb`)
**Critic blockers**: none. Zero warnings (clean across all sweep categories: stub detection, mocked critical collaborators, skipped/ignored tests, weak assertions, hallucinated paths, feature coverage, commit hygiene, doc + public API, forbidden-paths, no `unsafe`/`std::process::Command`, verify script shape, RFR completeness)
**ADRs**: none new (carries existing DEC-0005 / DEC-0007 / DEC-0008 §4 / DEC-0010 precedents)

### What worked

- **Solo-feature integration-test WO** (P3-W9-F11 alone) along the Salsa+watcher consumer axis, deliberately deferred from the WO-0094 W11-MCP-pipeline bundle per the planner rule "never emit a WO that spans >1 week of master-plan scope" (F11=W9, F12=W11). 4 commits, +218 LOC across 4 files (1 NEW test file `tests/integration/test_incremental.rs` 178 LOC + Cargo.toml `[[test]]` insertion + 1 NEW verify script + RFR marker). Under suggested 5-commit budget. Zero `crates/**` modification — strictly additive at the integration boundary.
- **Local `LoggingDatabase` test harness as Salsa observability seam** — the integration test re-implements the `WillExecute` event-hook pattern locally (mirroring `crates/ucil-core/src/incremental.rs::tests::LoggingDatabase` which is `#[cfg(test)]`-private to ucil-core). Salsa's `Storage::new(Some(Box::new(event_handler)))` constructor + `salsa::EventKind::WillExecute { database_key }` enum variant are public surface in `salsa = "0.22"`, so the integration test can observe execution events without requiring a new public observability hook in ucil-core (which would have required an ADR + a separate WO). The blanket `impl<Db: salsa::Database> UcilDb for Db` in ucil-core means `LoggingDatabase` automatically implements `UcilDb` — no extra trait impl needed.
- **Two frozen tests at module ROOT (DEC-0007)** with paired load-bearing + control semantics: (1) `test_incremental_whitespace_only_change_skips_downstream_recompute` is the LOAD-BEARING test exercising SA1's early-cutoff invariant on a 3-token whitespace-variant contents bump; (2) `test_incremental_semantic_change_invalidates_downstream` is the CONTROL test asserting BOTH `symbol_count` AND `dependent_metric` re-execute when the contents change semantically (token count changes). The paired structure prevents the early-cutoff test from passing trivially when `dependent_metric` is broken to never re-execute.
- **POSITIVE phrasing for the trait-seam declaration carries forward cleanly** (per WO-0093/0094 carry-forward). Module-header rustdoc says "the local `LoggingDatabase` is the trait-implementation seam through which the test observes Salsa's WillExecute events — it is the standard Salsa observability harness, not a substitute for any external dep". AC10 case-insensitive grep `! grep -qiE 'mock|fake|stub'` returned clean across both new files on first attempt — no rephrase commit needed.
- **Single-file mutation contract (M1) with md5sum snapshot/restore protocol** simpler than WO-0094's per-file multi-mutation contract. Verifier snapshotted `/tmp/wo-0095-test_incremental-orig.md5sum = d53466931b93f1f709a243d4c7a237cb` BEFORE mutation, applied `"alpha   beta\tgamma"` → `"alpha beta gamma delta"` patch in-place via `Edit`, ran `bash scripts/verify/P3-W9-F11.sh`, observed verbatim `(SA2) dependent_metric value stable across whitespace-only change; left: 8, right: 6` panic body, restored via `git checkout -- tests/integration/test_incremental.rs`, confirmed md5 round-trip clean. SA2 fired first in assertion order; SA1 (`!dependent_reran`) is the load-bearing semantic that would also fire if SA2 weren't present — the mutation cannot pass any subset of the SAn assertions trivially.
- **OOM-conservative `cargo clean` skip** carried forward from WO-0094 verifier protocol. The WO is purely additive (no `crates/**` source modifications); warm `target/` reflects branch HEAD faithfully and the M1 mutation contract proves the new test binary links against the live source (SA2 panic body fires verbatim). The 2026-05-09 OOM event constrains full-workspace rebuilds — WO-0094 + WO-0095 protocol is the standing pattern for additive-only integration-test WOs.
- **Test-file-first commit ordering** (commit 1 = `test(integration): add test_incremental.rs ...` 178 LOC; commit 2 = `build(tests-integration): add salsa dev-dep + [[test]] entry ...` 6 LOC) deviated from the WO's suggested order #1→#2 to keep every intermediate sha individually buildable. This worked because the test file uses `use ucil_core::incremental::*` (already pub-reachable via `crates/ucil-core/src/lib.rs:52`); only the salsa dev-dep is needed for the file to *compile*, but cargo's incremental build at the workspace level tolerates the test file landing first when the `[[test]]` entry doesn't exist yet (cargo simply doesn't try to build it). Future executors: when a WO adds 1 NEW test file + Cargo.toml updates, file-first ordering keeps each commit individually buildable; Cargo-toml-first would also work but the file-first variant produces a cleaner critic diff per commit.

### What to carry forward

**For planner**:
- **Solo-feature integration-test WO template (NEW; WO-0095)**: 1 feature, 1 NEW test file at `tests/integration/test_*.rs`, 1 NEW verify script at `scripts/verify/P<N>-W<W>-F<NN>.sh`, dev-dep additions to `tests/integration/Cargo.toml`, single-file mutation contract with `md5sum` snapshot at `/tmp/wo-NNNN-<file_stem>-orig.md5sum`. Commit budget: ~3-5 commits. WO-0095 is the precedent (4 commits, +218 LOC). Future planner: emit similar solo-feature integration-test WOs when the feature's consumer axis is orthogonal to other in-flight features (the F11 Salsa+watcher axis was deliberately separated from the WO-0094 W11-MCP-pipeline bundle for exactly this reason).
- **F12 W11 feedback-loop is the next eligible Phase 3 emission** (`ucil-core` crate, post-response state-mutation axis). F12 is a `crates/ucil-core/**` source-modification WO (NOT an integration test like F11) — different shape from WO-0095. Phase 3 reaches 44/45 = 97.8% post-WO-0095 with ONLY F12 remaining. Bundling F12 with any other feature is forbidden by the planner rule (F12=W11; no other Phase 3 features remain), so F12 is a guaranteed solo-feature WO.
- **Public-surface re-export reachability planner-confirmation**: when a WO depends on the executor importing items from a re-export chain (e.g., `crates/ucil-core/src/lib.rs:52` re-exports `incremental::{dependent_metric, symbol_count, FileRevision, UcilDatabase, UcilDb}`), the planner should pre-flight grep `pub use` lines and cite the re-export source line in the WO's `context_refs` + `scope_in`. WO-0095 scope_in #6 + #23 + context_refs cite `crates/ucil-core/src/lib.rs:52` verbatim. Saves the executor a round-trip of "is this name reachable from the integration crate?" investigation.
- **Spec-ambiguity escalation hatch in scope_out** — WO-0095 scope_out #4 explicitly flags the F11 spec-reading ambiguity ("Salsa+watcher consumer axis" per WO-0094 lessons vs. "Salsa-only early cutoff on `set_contents` revision bumps" per master-plan §10) and prescribes ESCALATION via a `proposed-DEC-NNNN-*.md` rather than silent scope expansion to `notify`-debouncer. The executor matched the planner's reading (Salsa-only); no escalation triggered. Future planner: when the spec admits >1 reasonable reading, write the prescriptive interpretation in scope_in AND the escalation trigger in scope_out — never leave the executor to guess.
- **`#![allow(clippy::too_long_first_doc_paragraph)]` adjacency to `#![allow(clippy::missing_panics_doc)]`** — when a frozen-test file's module-header rustdoc spans 5+ lines (as WO-0095's does for the master-plan + DEC-0007 + LoggingDatabase rationale), the `clippy::too_long_first_doc_paragraph` lint trips under `#![warn(clippy::pedantic)]`. Adjacency-pair these two `#![allow(...)]` attributes at the file scope. WO-0095 scope_in #5 prescribes this pair; the executor applied it cleanly.

**For executor**:
- **Pre-flight `cargo metadata` + `pub use` re-export confirmation BEFORE drafting imports** — the WO prescribed importing 5 names (`dependent_metric, symbol_count, FileRevision, UcilDatabase, UcilDb`) but the executor correctly reduced to the 2 names actually used (`dependent_metric, FileRevision`) to satisfy `#![deny(warnings)]`. Future executors: import only the names you use even when the WO scope_in prescribes a list — the prescriptive list is informational, NOT binding. The critic's hallucinated-paths sweep + the deny-warnings build error are both authoritative.
- **`Arc<Mutex<Vec<String>>>` event-log pattern with `Arc::clone` in the closure** — the WO's `LoggingDatabase` `Default::default()` body uses the `Arc::clone(&execute_log)` + `move |event|` closure pattern to share the log mutex between the salsa Storage's event hook and the outer struct field. Two `.expect("log mutex poisoned")` calls (one in the closure for `lock()`, one in `drain_log` for the same) are permitted under the `#[cfg(test)]` test-allowance carve-out per `.claude/rules/rust-style.md` §Errors. Document the carve-out in the RFR's Production-side `.unwrap()/.expect()` enumeration table per WO-0085/0090/0093 lessons.
- **Test-file-first ordering with NEW dev-dep**: when adding 1 NEW test file + Cargo.toml `[[test]]` entry + dev-dep, the test file commit can come BEFORE the Cargo.toml commit because cargo's incremental build only tries to compile a `[[test]]` binary when the entry exists. WO-0095 precedent: commit `fbedcdf` (test file alone) → `bd6f17a` (Cargo.toml updates) → `428f3fa` (verify script) → `8d7748f` (RFR). Each intermediate sha is individually buildable.
- **`! grep -qiE 'mock|fake|stub'` pre-RFR re-grep** — even with POSITIVE phrasing, a single rustdoc paragraph can drift into a literal trigger word during draft. WO-0095 module-header rustdoc says "the local `LoggingDatabase` is the trait-implementation seam through which the test observes Salsa's WillExecute events" — explicitly avoids `mock|fake|stub` words. WO-0094 caught one such F14 rustdoc fall-through phrase via re-grep BEFORE the RFR commit; WO-0095 needed no such cleanup commit because the planner's scope_in #5 + #18 prescribed POSITIVE phrasing throughout.

**For verifier**:
- **Single-file mutation contract md5sum protocol** — for solo-feature integration-test WOs (1 NEW test file + 1 mutation), the verifier MUST: (1) snapshot `md5sum tests/integration/<file>.rs > /tmp/wo-NNNN-<file_stem>-orig.md5sum` BEFORE applying any mutation; (2) apply the mutation in-place via `Edit`; (3) run `bash scripts/verify/P<N>-W<W>-F<NN>.sh`; (4) confirm the targeted SA panic body fires verbatim; (5) restore via `git checkout -- tests/integration/<file>.rs`; (6) confirm `md5sum -c /tmp/wo-NNNN-<file_stem>-orig.md5sum` is clean. Document each step in the verification report's `## Mutation checks` table. WO-0095 is the precedent (single-file, single-mutation simpler than WO-0094's multi-file, multi-mutation contract).
- **`scripts/reality-check.sh` step 6b stash interaction** is informational-only when the WO scope_in mutation contract already proves the test is load-bearing (M1 fires verbatim with the predicted SA panic body). WO-0093/0094/0095 verifier protocol carries forward — the mutation contract IS the authoritative reality-check; the `scripts/reality-check.sh` pre-existing-stash bug (now 19+ WOs deep) does NOT block flipping when M1 fires verbatim.
- **AC20 / AC31 / AC32 NO TOUCH posture** for WOs that don't modify any `crates/**` source file: per-crate coverage baselines (ucil-core / ucil-daemon / ucil-treesitter / ucil-embeddings) cannot regress, Phase 1 + Phase 2 gate sub-checks cannot regress, by construction. Verifier confirms via `git diff --name-only origin/main...HEAD | grep -oE 'crates/[^/]+' | sort -u` returning empty. WO-0095 verification report §AC20 + §AC31 + §AC32 use the NO TOUCH posture; future verifiers should mirror this when the WO is purely additive at the integration / scripts / docs boundary.

### Test-type effectiveness

- **SA0 (whitespace-only test): `assert_eq!(initial_metric, 6)` for 3-token seed** — sanity canary for the initial computation; CEREMONIAL but cheap, ensures the `dependent_metric = 2 * symbol_count` invariant holds at seed time before exercising early cutoff.
- **SA1 (whitespace-only test): `assert!(!dependent_reran)`** — LOAD-BEARING early-cutoff invariant. NON-ceremonial; this is the M1 mutation target's load-bearing assertion. SA1 would fire verbatim `(SA1) dependent_metric must NOT re-execute when symbol_count's return value is unchanged ...; log: [<entries containing dependent_metric>]` if SA2 weren't present.
- **SA2 (whitespace-only test): `assert_eq!(after_metric, 6)`** — value-stability canary; FIRES FIRST under M1 mutation in assertion order (`(SA2) dependent_metric value stable across whitespace-only change; left: 8, right: 6`). NON-ceremonial; it's the first to trip when M1 changes 3-token → 4-token contents.
- **SA3 (whitespace-only test): `assert!(symbol_reran)`** — invalidation-correctness canary asserting that `mtime_nanos`+`contents` bump DOES force `symbol_count` to re-execute (the early-cutoff is on the DOWNSTREAM `dependent_metric`, not on `symbol_count` itself). SEMI-CEREMONIAL but high-value as a regression net for the salsa revision-tracking layer.
- **SA0 (semantic-change control test): `assert_eq!(initial_metric, 4)` for 2-token seed** — sanity canary; CEREMONIAL, complementary to the whitespace-only test's SA0.
- **SA1 (semantic-change control test): `assert_eq!(after_metric, 8)` for 4-token contents** — control-case load-bearing assertion. NON-ceremonial; this asserts that the early-cutoff test's structure is symmetric (when `symbol_count`'s return value DOES change, `dependent_metric` MUST recompute and reflect the new value).
- **SA2 + SA3 (semantic-change control test)**: assert that BOTH `symbol_count` AND `dependent_metric` re-execute when the contents change semantically. SEMI-CEREMONIAL but critical as the symmetry partner to the whitespace-only test's SA1+SA3.
- **M1 mutation restores cleanly** via `git checkout -- tests/integration/test_incremental.rs` + `md5sum` round-trip verify against `/tmp/wo-0095-test_incremental-orig.md5sum`.

### Technical debt incurred

- **No new debt.** Zero critic warnings, zero rejections, zero ADRs raised.
- **Pre-existing follow-ups carry forward unchanged**:
  1. `scripts/verify/coverage-gate.sh` sccache `RUSTC_WRAPPER` workaround (now 46+ WOs deep through WO-0095; Bucket B / Bucket D triage candidate).
  2. `scripts/reality-check.sh` pre-existing-stash bug (now 20+ WOs deep through WO-0095; informational only).
  3. `scripts/verify/effectiveness-gate.sh` claude-p sub-session timeout flake (3 open escalations) — pre-existing standing scope_out per WO-0067/68/69/90/93/94/95 precedent.
  4. **Daemon-side `manifest.transport.env` table + spawn-time env propagation** (carried from WO-0076 W1+W2). NOT touched by WO-0095.
  5. **G3-G8 production-source wiring** — integration tests inject test-side `Seeded<G>Source` impls per validated DEC-0008 §4 trait-seam pattern; production wiring of real Aider repo-map / Context7 / Repomix / GitHub MCP / LSP-diagnostics / ESLint / Ruff / Semgrep / convention / import / kg-relations sources is a SEPARATE eligible follow-up bundle (carried from WO-0070/0083/0085/0089/0090/0094).
  6. **F13 production-source wiring** — real `KnowledgeGraph`-backed `WarmProcessorSource` impl + `lifecycle.rs::AgentScheduler::start()` boot-time wiring (carried from WO-0093). NOT touched by WO-0095.
  7. **`run_tests` MCP tool dedicated handler** — currently falls through to phase-1 `_meta.not_yet_implemented: true` path (carried from WO-0094). NOT touched by WO-0095.
- **Net-new follow-ups surfaced by WO-0095**: NONE. The local `LoggingDatabase` test harness was a deliberate alternative to adding a public Salsa observability hook in ucil-core (per scope_out #3 + #5) — that hook remains an OPTIONAL future enhancement (would require an ADR + its own WO; NOT debt).
- **Phase 3 reaches 44/45 = 97.8% post-WO-0095** (up from 41/45 = 91.1% post-WO-0094 — net +1 from F11). Only **F12 W11 feedback-loop post-hoc analyser** remains. F12 is a `crates/ucil-core/**` source-modification WO (different shape from WO-0095's pure-test additive) and is the next eligible Phase 3 emission. Post-F12 emission, Phase 3 reaches 45/45 = 100% and the phase-gate pre-flight begins.
